<Text>I've read positive and negative reviews for Norco Donut. I completely agree with the positive ones and completely disagree with the negative ones. If I have one complaint at all, its that they sell out of my favorite donuts often before I can get there. Not their fault of course, their donuts are way better than anyone else's!

The two women who operate the shop have always been incredibly friendly and shown exemplary customer service. I have placed orders that have come back incorrect - and they have made the whole order over again from scratch WITHOUT me paying for it again. They have taken the time to get to know my family, and even know what we like.

To the food quality, I can only speak to the donuts and sandwiches. I have found both to be fresh and delicious every time. The donuts are always made from scratch daily. Down the street a half-mile or so is a Yum Yum Donuts store. We have purchased from both stores and we now consider Norco Donut our donut store. Yum Yum doesn't even compare - their donuts are stale and tasteless!

Norco Donut has been around for a few years. Anything they screwed up at the beginning is well fixed now. They do a great job and I hope they stay in business for many years to come.</Text><Response>None</Response>< date>

< review>
Trains are pretty clean and reasonable for working in with a laptop, except for the few that are packed.  Most of the tracks are shared with freight trains, so there are occasional delays and cancelled trains.  Metrolink does a good job on safety since a driver crashed a train a decade ago.

Ticket Prices are way out of control.  The saving calculations Metrolink provides only make sense if your vehicle gets poor mileage, you pay through the nose for your vehicle maintainance, and you have to pay for parking at your destination.  If you buy a monthly pass and ride the train everyday, then the cost gets a little more reasonable.  (Yet who really rides it every day?)  Metrolink use to have a 10 pass deal, which made sense.  Wish they would bring that back.</review>

<user>115363957132542990988</user><date>1444145650417</date>< Text>
Effective 10/5/15 Metrolink reduced service on the San Bernardino - Los Angeles line and materially changed the train schedule. Both yesterday and today trains were packed during normal commute times and trains ran behind schedule as a result of the additional time needed by passengers to exit and board cars that were packed to capacity with riders crowded together in the aisles. Those type of delays compound as each stop adds to the accumulated delays. This morning, the train that was supposed to arrive in Covina at 6:53 AM was about 15 minutes late as a result of the in-station delays that occurred during the trip from San Bernardino.

What's sadly laughable is that Metrolink preceded this change with an announcement of "Enhanced" service. The changes were hardly an enhancement and calling them such is rather insulting. I suppose the marketing department couldn't bring themselves to issue a release with the headline "Metrolink to boost profits by reducing service, combined with proposed fare increases."<//Text>

<gmapID>0x80dcb73630959e21:0xae84e6030a9add1c<//gmapID>< Text>
This is such a delightful store! It has everything you need to decorate your backyard for feeding birds & critters. Such pretty feeders that I had to get multiples. There are many beautiful & whimsical birdbaths; I must buy one soon. The owners & staff are always very friendly & knowledgeable. They are enthusiastic to help find the right feeders & accessories for your needs. I highly recommend to join their club. I think it's $25 for a year. It gives great discounts on your purchases and you can receive $10 in birdbucks to spend in the store. Every month I spend at least $150, and I get $10 in birdbucks which I used the following month. Sure you can buy cheaper bags of birdseed from big chain discount stores, but those bags are full of extra fillers that aren't eaten. For quality mixes of birdseed that doesn't go to waste and for excellent customer service, Wild Birds Unlimited is the best choice. It is a local small business that deserves our support.< /Text>

None<//Response>
< Text>
Everyone's different, I get it. I came in with low expectations - actually expecting to be turned away too with how bad my credit and history was, but also with a sliver of hope that they can help me. I've been in contact with Abraham & Dayshawn for a couple weeks, I gave them my story and application filled out online and we made an appointment for me to come in after the new year.

I showed up with the documents required ready for Dayshawn & team to review, they entered everything and in about 10-15 minutes of dealing with the bank and whoever, Aric the Sales Manager introduced himself and led me to their lot for what they could offer me based on my preferred monthly payment and what they were selling. So it's a bit backwards - in that they get all your information first and see what you qualify for, and give you the options, versus other dealerships where you go in picking a car thinking you can get it only to be turned down for whatever reason and then having to settle on a lesser model or whatever.

Once I was happy with the car I chose after a quick test drive which always involves going a circle back to the dealership (in this case, a series of left turns lol but at least there was some road interference: railroad tracks, small dips and hills to go up and long stretches of industrial park roads to really test acceleration and torque), we then came back to discuss final numbers.

This is where other dealerships would differ - CarCredit already has the general number for you based on what you want, not the other way around. Now it's just paperwork of filling out the DMV registration form and the long car finance form, submitting my down payment with Rachelle, and all that other jazz.

In the meantime, my car was getting washed and cleaned up, got my keys and I was done. Total time spent was about 3 hours - which is expected and about average I'd say.

I'd like to extend my thanks to the team for helping me out and getting me in a car when everyone else told me no.<//Text>

< user_id>
104610606609028420762<//user_id>
<pictures>None<//pictures>< review>
Very strange McDonalds. It is attached to a gas station where you can enter through the gas station door or the McDonald's door and end up in the same space. It's not one of those places that has a very good parking lot. In fact when I first came here I actually thought it was a drive through because I didn't see any parking spaces for McDonald's patrons to park. Just before heading out, I finally found approximately 10 spaces tuck into the far corner by the drive-thru that didn't appear to belong to the gas station. Because of their they are pretty difficult to get into, and almost impossible to get out of.
The entire place is really not that clean. I have been here almost an hour and in that time no one has cleaned any of the tables or cleaned the garbage off of the floors.
They do have a pretty steady clientele mostly the drive-thru but many that walk in. Their menu seems complete. Prices are about the same across the board as other McDonald's I have visited. Yes, they do have high chairs!
The personnel seemed extremely pleasant. They tend to talk to each other well, get the job done and in a reasonable time. This is truly a fast food restaurant, the wait here is very short.
If you're looking for quiet, this is not the place to come. There's a lot of noise that comes from the gas station part of the building, the road that runs right beside the building, the drive-through and just the traffic of McDonald's workers and patrons themself.
Would I come back here? Actually I would. There's nothing here that scares me off. I feel safe, I feel secure, and the food was McDonald's food. Isn't that what I walked in for?
If you enjoyed my review, please LIKE below and, as always, have an amazing day!<//review>
